- What changed: Added `describeTerminalDebugText` in `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts` (with tests) to render control characters and spaces in a log-safe readable form (`<DEL>`, `<SP>`, `<CR>`, etc.). Wired detailed realtime input diagnostics in `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` across keypress reception, text change delta derivation, buffer enqueue/flush, queue dispatch, and retry/error paths under `[ghodex-input]` log tags.
- Why: Backspace still mutates into spaces on specific Android keyboard + hidden-input paths. We need an end-to-end observable event chain to identify exactly where the wrong payload is introduced.
- Impact: With `adb logcat`, each user key action now exposes deterministic input-state transitions and emitted terminal payloads, so root-cause analysis is no longer guesswork.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `adb logcat -s ReactNativeJS | grep ghodex-input`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep diagnostics local to the mobile input coordinator and avoid protocol churn. Structured runtime logs provide immediate field evidence without altering gateway contracts.

### fix(happy-client): stop Android IME backspace from injecting spaces in realtime terminal mode

- What changed: Extended realtime input delta handling in `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts` with a `backspaceKeypressHint` fallback so whitespace-only insertions immediately after a backspace keypress are treated as synthetic IME artifacts and ignored. Updated `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` to pass a short backspace hint window and normalize key detection (`backspace/delete/del`) case-insensitively before enqueueing terminal payloads. Added regression coverage in `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts` for the zero-delete Android path (`pending=0 + backspace hint + whitespace insertion`).
- Why: On some Android keyboards, backspace in hidden realtime capture input can report a whitespace insertion instead of a delete delta, which made the terminal receive spaces when users pressed backspace.
- Impact: System keyboard backspace in realtime mode no longer degrades into space insertion on affected Android IMEs; typing and erase behavior stays aligned with terminal expectations.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; on-device realtime terminal manual check with system keyboard backspace.
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the fix local to mobile input normalization and avoid protocol changes. A bounded backspace hint from keypress events is the smallest reliable way to reject IME ghost whitespace without changing normal text streaming semantics.

### fix(happy-client): switch realtime terminal to viewport-first input and serialize gateway writes

- What changed: Updated realtime terminal interaction in `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` to remove the visible bottom composer in realtime mode and capture typing via a hidden terminal-focus input (`tap viewport -> keyboard -> direct stream`). Realtime control keys and text now share one serialized mutation queue with bounded retry on `session_limit_exceeded`, and subscription-driven live reads are deferred while writes are in flight. Realtime quick-key strip no longer renders the standalone `⌫` button; Backspace is now expected from the system keyboard key path.
- Why: The previous split path could blur/focus the keyboard repeatedly around quick-key taps, and mixed concurrent read/write requests could exceed gateway per-identity session concurrency (`Gateway concurrent session limit exceeded`), especially during fast typing.
- Impact: Realtime mode now behaves closer to SSH interaction on mobile: no bottom text box, terminal-first typing flow, reduced keyboard flicker, and much lower chance of gateway concurrent-session errors during high-frequency input.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client/android && ANDROID_HOME=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ANDROID_SDK_ROOT=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ./gradlew --no-daemon installDebug -PreactNativeArchitectures=arm64-v8a`; on-device manual check: realtime mode tap terminal to type, hold rapid input/backspace, verify keyboard stability and no repeated `session_limit_exceeded` error.
- Files: `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep protocol changes minimal and solve UX + stability in the mobile coordinator layer: one writer lane for realtime mutations, defer competing reads during write bursts, and remove the dedicated realtime backspace button once keyboard key path is available.

### fix(happy-client): keep realtime keyboard stable on control keys and restore visible caret

- What changed: Updated mobile workspace terminal input in `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` so realtime mode no longer hides the input caret, control-key strip taps use `keyboardShouldPersistTaps="always"` / `keyboardDismissMode="none"`, and control-key sends now refocus the realtime input after dispatch.
- Why: In realtime mode, tapping quick keys like Backspace could blur the input and collapse the keyboard, and hidden-caret behavior made typing state hard to track.
- Impact: Realtime terminal interaction is smoother: keyboard stays up during quick-key operations and input cursor is visible while typing.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client/android && ANDROID_HOME=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ANDROID_SDK_ROOT=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ./gradlew --no-daemon installDebug -PreactNativeArchitectures=arm64-v8a`; `adb shell am force-stop com.leongong.ghodex.remote.dev && adb shell monkey -p com.leongong.ghodex.remote.dev -c android.intent.category.LAUNCHER 1`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the existing realtime transport protocol unchanged and fix UX at the input layer first. Focus-retention plus visible-caret restoration is the smallest safe change that addresses both keyboard flicker and editing clarity.

### fix(macos): prevent dock icon plugin from mutating transient build app bundles

- What changed: Added `AppBundleIconMutationPolicy.shouldWriteBundleIcon(at:)` in `macos/Sources/Features/Custom App Icon/AppIcon.swift` and switched `DockTilePlugin` icon writes to honor this policy. The plugin now skips `NSWorkspace.setIcon(... forFile:)` and filesystem change notifications when the enclosing app bundle path is under Xcode transient outputs (`/DerivedData/` or `/Build/Products/`). Added `macos/Tests/DockTilePluginTests.swift` with explicit coverage for DerivedData rejection, Build/Products rejection, and installed `/Applications/*.app` allow.
- Why: Writing custom bundle icons inside test/build artifacts creates Finder metadata (`Icon\r`, FinderInfo/resource-fork style detritus) that can break later `codesign` phases and produce flaky macOS test/build gates.
- Impact: macOS test/build loops are more stable, especially for repeated `xcodebuild test` runs that re-sign app artifacts. Installed app bundles still keep user-facing dock icon behavior.
- Verification: `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -destination 'platform=macOS,arch=arm64' -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-sendkey-focused -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/DockTilePluginTests test`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -destination 'platform=macOS,arch=arm64' -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-sendkey-focused -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests '-only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/sendKeyUsesDedicatedKeyExecutionPath()' '-only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/sendKeyIsSupportedMutationCommand()' '-only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/runCommandUsesDedicatedExecutionPath()' '-only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/sendTextRejectsMissingTerminalWithoutEmittingEvents()' test`
- Files: `macos/Sources/Features/Custom App Icon/AppIcon.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Custom App Icon/DockTilePlugin.swift`, `macos/Tests/DockTilePluginTests.swift`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep dock-icon behavior unchanged for real installed apps, but treat build/test app bundles as immutable artifacts. The lowest-risk fix is a path-based write guard at the shared icon-mutation boundary rather than broad plugin behavior changes.

### fix(ghodex): stabilize realtime mobile terminal key-stream writes and backspace behavior

- What changed: Kept realtime buffered `send-text` drain for normal typing, but switched mobile control-strip keys to a dedicated `send-key` mutation path with `send-text` fallback for older desktop builds. Added new gateway API `sendTerminalKey` on mobile and new desktop command `send-key` (`terminal_key`) in Control Harness, wired to native `sendKeyEvent` (Enter/Backspace/Tab/Esc/ArrowUp/ArrowDown/Ctrl+C/Ctrl+D). Added server/client tests to lock the new protocol contract. Also aligned realtime backspace payload handling to `DEL (0x7F)` across keypress and delta-diff paths.
- Why: Character injection (`send-text`) is not equivalent to real key events for many terminal states, so shortcut buttons could drift from expected behavior (especially backspace/enter/arrows). A protocol-level key-event path is required for deterministic mapping.
- Impact: Bottom quick buttons now map to actual terminal key events, reducing misfires and mode-dependent behavior. Backspace behavior is consistent with common shell erase defaults, and old paired desktops remain usable through `send-text` fallback.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts sources/ghodex/storage.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-send-key-deriveddata -destination 'platform=macOS,arch=arm64' -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/sendKeyUsesDedicatedKeyExecutionPath -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/runCommandUsesDedicatedExecutionPath -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/sendTextRejectsMissingTerminalWithoutEmittingEvents test`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts`, `macos/Sources/App/macOS/AppDelegate.swift`, `macos/Sources/Ghostty/Surface View/SurfaceView_AppKit.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessCore.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessGateway.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessSupport.swift`, `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep simple mode semantics unchanged; scope this fix to realtime mode transport behavior. Replace per-key round trips with buffered serial writes first (lower protocol pressure, better responsiveness) and keep terminal refresh responsibility on existing live-update/poll paths instead of forcing per-key write-settle reads.

### feat(ghodex): add mobile terminal input-mode switch and restore execute-on-send semantics

- What changed: Added a new local setting `mobileTerminalInputMode` (`simple` / `realtime`) in `happy-client/sources/sync/localSettings.ts` and exposed it in `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/index.tsx` as a tap-to-toggle item under app settings. Added `resolveTerminalSubmitMutation` in `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts` with tests in `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts` so simple-mode single-line sends route to `run-command` (execute immediately), while multiline continues to use `send-text` as raw paste. Updated `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` to consume this mode routing, show realtime-mode hint copy, and add realtime key-stream handling (`onKeyPress`) that forwards printable keys, Enter, Backspace, and Tab directly through `send-text`.
- Why: The previous unified send path favored `send-text`, which could leave commands only entered in terminal input without immediate execution on some desktop paths. Users also needed an explicit choice between low-friction command submission and SSH-like direct key streaming.
- Impact: Default simple mode now behaves like the original “send and execute” flow, while realtime mode provides direct key-forward interaction without removing the existing simple workflow.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts sources/ghodex/storage.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/sync/localSettings.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/index.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep backward-compatible UX by defaulting to `simple`, restore deterministic execute-on-send via `run-command` for single-line submissions, and keep realtime mode opt-in until broader IME/input-method compatibility is fully validated across devices.

### fix(ghodex): prevent mobile startup stalls on SecureStore and disable default debug packager probing

- What changed: Updated `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts` so native session writes are timeout-bounded and first-launch default-session persistence no longer blocks `loadStoredSession` readiness. Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.spec.ts` regression coverage for unresolved SecureStore write/read paths during bootstrap. Updated `happy-client/android/app/build.gradle` and `happy-client/android/app/src/main/java/com/leongong/ghodex/remote/dev/MainApplication.kt` to gate React developer support behind `BuildConfig.ENABLE_DEV_SUPPORT` (default `false`, overridable with `-Pghodex.enableDevSupport=true`) so install-debug test builds no longer attempt Metro packager probing by default.
- Why: On some devices, SecureStore operations can hang during cold start, which kept workspace `loaded` false and looked like a permanent splash/launch freeze. In parallel, debug dev-support probing still attempted local packager websocket checks that were unnecessary for embedded-bundle test installs.
- Impact: Mobile cold start no longer blocks indefinitely on SecureStore persistence, and default phone test installs are self-contained without `localhost:8081` packager dependency.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/storage.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client/android && ANDROID_HOME=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ANDROID_SDK_ROOT=/Users/leongong/Library/Android/sdk ./gradlew --no-daemon installDebug -PreactNativeArchitectures=arm64-v8a`; `adb shell am force-stop com.leongong.ghodex.remote.dev && adb shell monkey -p com.leongong.ghodex.remote.dev -c android.intent.category.LAUNCHER 1`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.spec.ts`, `happy-client/android/app/build.gradle`, `happy-client/android/app/src/main/java/com/leongong/ghodex/remote/dev/MainApplication.kt`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep bootstrap resilient by making persistence best-effort after a bounded timeout rather than a hard startup dependency, and keep debug packager support opt-in so default QA installs prioritize reliable offline launch behavior.

### feat(ghodex): add mobile terminal RTT badge and direct TTY control-key input

- What changed: Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.ts` plus `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalInput.spec.ts` as the shared mobile terminal input/latency helper surface (single-line payload auto-Enter, multiline raw send, control-key payload catalog, bounded latency sampling). Updated `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` so workspace requests now record gateway RTT samples, terminal toolbar shows a live RTT badge, the command dock sends text through `send-text` by default (with `run-command` fallback only for older unsupported gateways), and a dedicated mobile control-key strip now sends `Enter`, `Ctrl+C`, `Ctrl+D`, `Esc`, `Tab`, and arrow keys directly to the TTY.
- Why: Command-only submission was too restrictive for interactive terminal workflows (slash commands, interrupt signals, cursor-navigation editing). The mobile client needed first-class TTY-style input controls and visible network latency feedback without waiting for desktop-side tooling.
- Impact: Phone-side terminal interaction now behaves closer to a real terminal keyboard for common control sequences, and users can see live request latency (`RTT`) directly in the workspace toolbar while operating over LAN or relay.

- Decision trail: Keep the change mobile-local and protocol-compatible. Reuse existing `send-text` mutation as the primary path to preserve interactive TTY semantics, add a compatibility fallback for older gateways, and expose latency as a lightweight in-memory rolling RTT badge rather than introducing a new metrics backend.

### fix(ghodex): bootstrap first-pair relay connectivity from QR metadata

- What changed: Extended desktop pairing QR payloads to optionally include `public_endpoint` plus preferred transport metadata when a valid public gateway endpoint is configured. Extended `happy-client` QR parsing to preserve those optional fields with backward compatibility for existing LAN payloads, and added relay/LAN attempt ordering so scanned pairing can try relay first (or LAN first when requested) with automatic fallback before failing.
- Why: Non-LAN first-time pairing failed because QR bootstrap only carried LAN host/port data, so mobile attempted an unreachable private socket before it had relay metadata from pairing exchange.
- Impact: Off-LAN users can now complete first pairing through the configured relay endpoint directly from QR, while mixed environments still retain LAN fallback behavior and legacy QR payload compatibility.

- Decision trail: Keep relay bootstrap additive to the existing QR contract. Carry optional relay hints in QR, preserve old parsing behavior, and enforce deterministic relay/LAN retry ordering on the mobile side so pairing no longer depends on a reachable LAN path.

### fix(ghodex): preserve terminal ANSI styling in desktop-to-mobile read path

- What changed: Added a VT-preserving surface read export (`ghostty_surface_read_text_vt`) in the embedded runtime (`src/apprt/embedded.zig`) plus format-aware selection output plumbing (`src/terminal/Screen.zig`, `src/Surface.zig`) and C header updates (`include/ghodex.h`, `macos/GhoDexKit.xcframework/**/Headers/ghodex.h`). Updated `macos/Sources/Ghostty/Surface View/SurfaceView_AppKit.swift` to add dedicated control-harness VT read caches and switched `ControlHarnessReadableSurface` (`macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessSampleStore.swift`) to those VT reads. Added `readTerminalDeltaPreservesAnsiRowsForMobileRenderer` in `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift` to lock ANSI row preservation through `snapshot` -> `delta`. Rebuilt `macos/GhoDexKit.xcframework` so the new symbol is available to the app target.
- Why: The mobile renderer already supported ANSI segments, but desktop `read-terminal` sampling was sourced from plain text extraction, so style data was stripped before the payload reached mobile. This made real-device output appear as uniformly white text even though renderer logic was present.
- Impact: `read-terminal` payloads for mobile control-harness paths now preserve ANSI/SGR styling, allowing the existing row renderer to display foreground/background/emphasis colors correctly. Newline normalization (`\r\n` -> `\n`) keeps row indexes stable for delta merge semantics.

### feat(ghodex): switch the mobile terminal viewport to a row-based renderer

- What changed: Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/model.ts` plus `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/model.spec.ts` to turn ANSI parsing into a reusable row-model helper with incremental row-patch support. Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/TerminalRenderer.tsx` and updated `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` so the workspace now stores parsed terminal rows beside authoritative `terminalContent`, rebuilds rows on snapshot reads, applies only touched rows on merge-safe delta reads, and renders the main terminal viewport through a list-based row renderer instead of a single giant text block. `happy-client/sources/ghodex/ansi.tsx` now reuses the same row parser as the fallback helper path. The renderer boundary and verification result are recorded in `ghodex-mobile-spec-09-mobile-terminal-renderer.md`, and the execution update in `happy-client-mobile-plan.md` now marks `SPEC-09` complete.
- Why: `SPEC-08` made the delta transport safe, but the main mobile UI still reparsed and rendered terminal content as one large ANSI text block on every refresh. The next coherent step is a row-based renderer that can consume safe deltas incrementally without dragging `SPEC-10` metrics or observability work into the change.
- Impact: The main workspace terminal view is now row-based, theme-aware by default terminal colors, and structurally ready for smoother long-output rendering. Safe delta updates no longer require reparsing untouched rows, while authoritative terminal text remains intact for compatibility and fallback paths.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminal/model.spec.ts sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.spec.ts sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/model.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/model.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminal/TerminalRenderer.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/ansi.tsx`, `ghodex-mobile-spec-09-mobile-terminal-renderer.md`, `happy-client-mobile-plan.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the renderer upgrade narrowly scoped to mobile row modeling and list rendering. Preserve `terminalContent` as the authoritative string, use parsed rows as a derived cache, and stop before metrics, latency counters, or cursor/search UX that belong to `SPEC-10`.

### feat(ghodex): harden terminal delta transport safety and fallback rules

- What changed: Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.ts` plus `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.spec.ts` to isolate delta-merge decisions from the workspace screen. The new helper makes row-delta application deterministic for mixed `update` and `delete` patches, codifies when the mobile client may request delta at all, and forces snapshot fallback when lineage or patch completeness is unsafe. `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx` now consumes that helper so truncated local terminal buffers no longer attempt to merge absolute desktop row indexes. On desktop, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessCore.swift` now preserves the full `changed_rows` set for delta reads instead of silently trimming it with the snapshot `maxLines` budget, and `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift` now locks both the complete-delta and evicted-frame reset contracts. The transport boundary, deferrals, and verification outcome are recorded in `ghodex-mobile-spec-08-terminal-transport-upgrade.md`, and the execution update in `happy-client-mobile-plan.md` now marks `SPEC-08` complete.
- Why: The repo already had frame ids and row deltas, but the transport contract was still unsafe in two specific places: mobile could merge deltas against truncated local buffers, and desktop could advertise mergeable row patches after truncating `changed_rows` with a snapshot-oriented line budget. Those edge cases belong in the transport layer, not in the later renderer rewrite.
- Impact: Incremental terminal reads are now safer and more predictable. Merge-safe local buffers continue to use delta, incompatible lineage still resyncs through snapshot, and the desktop no longer emits partial row diffs that can corrupt mobile terminal content.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.spec.ts sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-spec08-focused-deriveddata -destination 'platform=macOS' -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/readTerminalDeltaPreservesCompleteChangedRowsWhenMaxLinesIsSmall -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/readTerminalDeltaFallsBackToResetWhenSinceFrameWasEvicted test`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/terminalTransport.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessCore.swift`, `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift`, `ghodex-mobile-spec-08-terminal-transport-upgrade.md`, `happy-client-mobile-plan.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep `SPEC-08` strictly about transport correctness. Delta is allowed only when the mobile side holds a merge-safe base frame, and any incomplete or incompatible patch falls back to snapshot. Leave renderer replacement and visual optimization to `SPEC-09`.

### feat(ghodex): add desktop device registry and device-scoped revoke control

- What changed: Extended the mobile pairing contract so `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts` and `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx` now send the persisted phone `deviceId` and `deviceLabel` during `gateway.pairing.begin`, and added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts` to lock that contract. On desktop, `ControlHarnessCore.swift` now decodes `device_id` / `device_label`, `ControlHarnessAuth.swift` now persists a device registry beside desktop identity and token state, and `ControlHarnessGateway.swift` now exposes local-only `gateway.devices.list` and `gateway.devices.revoke` commands. Registry rows track the durable device id, display label, trust state, last seen, last transport mode, and forward-compatible capability flags, while live connection state is derived from the gateway session registry. Device revoke is wired through token invalidation plus active-stream shutdown so the registry is not just informational. The durable design and verification outcome are recorded in `ghodex-mobile-spec-07-desktop-device-registry.md`, and the plan execution update in `happy-client-mobile-plan.md` now marks `SPEC-07` complete.
- Why: `SPEC-08` and later renderer/transport work need a desktop-authoritative notion of which phone is paired, trusted, currently connected, and revocable. The smallest coherent way to add that without building a UI first is to have the desktop own a registry keyed by the phone's stable device id and expose list/revoke commands for local desktop management and testability.
- Impact: The desktop can now enumerate known paired phones, show live vs idle state, and revoke one phone without invalidating unrelated devices. Existing older auth files continue to work because the registry backfills from persisted token subjects, and older clients without explicit device identity remain pairable through a fallback subject-based registry identity.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-spec07-focused-deriveddata -destination 'platform=macOS' -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authPairingExchangeReturnsStableDesktopIdentity -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authRestoresDesktopIdentityAcrossReload -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayPairingLifecycleIssuesRotatesAndRevokesTokens -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayPairingLifecyclePublishesRelayMetadataWhenPublicEndpointIsConfigured -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayDeviceRegistryListsKnownDevicesAndPersistsAcrossReload -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayDeviceRegistryRevokesOnlyTargetDeviceAndClosesActiveStreams test`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.spec.ts`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessCore.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessAuth.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessGateway.swift`, `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift`, `ghodex-mobile-spec-07-desktop-device-registry.md`, `happy-client-mobile-plan.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep registry ownership in desktop auth persistence instead of creating a second store, treat live connection state as derived gateway state rather than a separate persisted field, and make revoke meaningful by tying it directly to both token invalidation and active-stream shutdown. That preserves a clean boundary for later desktop UI and richer transport work.

### feat(ghodex): add encrypted public gateway transport metadata and framing

- What changed: Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/transport.ts` plus `happy-client/sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts` to resolve LAN vs relay socket URLs and to encode/decode AES-GCM public transport envelopes around the existing gateway JSON protocol. Updated `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/types.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/sessionState.ts`, and `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx` so pairing exchange and token rotation can persist `publicEndpoint`, `transportSharedSecret`, and relay transport metadata, and so request/subscribe flows automatically encrypt only the public `wss://` path while keeping LAN behavior unchanged. On desktop, `ControlHarnessAuth.swift` now issues and persists a per-token `transport_shared_secret` with backward-compatible decode for older persisted auth state, `ControlHarnessGateway.swift` now publishes relay metadata when a valid public endpoint is configured and uses the shared secret to decrypt `gateway.encrypted` requests plus encrypt outbound responses/events, and `ControlHarnessGatewaySecureChannel.swift` provides the shared AES-GCM framing helper used by both request and envelope paths. Added focused desktop coverage for secure-channel round trips and public endpoint metadata publication, and recorded the design/verification outcome in `ghodex-mobile-spec-06-public-network-encrypted-connectivity.md` plus the execution update in `happy-client-mobile-plan.md`.
- Why: The plan needed a public-network connectivity step before desktop registry and richer terminal transport work, but this repo does not yet contain a hosted relay service. The smallest coherent slice is to preserve the current LAN control protocol, add an optional public `wss://` endpoint descriptor, and protect that public path with application-layer encryption instead of inventing a second transport protocol prematurely.
- Impact: Paired devices can now carry relay-ready transport metadata without losing LAN compatibility, public transport no longer exposes plaintext control payloads when the gateway is reachable through an external `wss://` endpoint, and older persisted desktop auth state migrates forward without forcing the user to re-pair just to gain the new secure-channel contract.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts sources/sync/settings.spec.ts sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-spec06-focused-deriveddata -destination 'platform=macOS' -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authExpiresPairingCodesAndPersistsIssuedTokens -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authPairingExchangeReturnsStableDesktopIdentity -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authRestoresDesktopIdentityAcrossReload -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewaySecureChannelRoundTripsEncryptedRequest -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewaySecureChannelRoundTripsEncryptedEnvelope -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayPairingLifecycleIssuesRotatesAndRevokesTokens -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/gatewayPairingLifecyclePublishesRelayMetadataWhenPublicEndpointIsConfigured test`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/ghodex/transport.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/transport.spec.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/types.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/sessionState.ts`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessAuth.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessGateway.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessGatewaySecureChannel.swift`, `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift`, `ghodex-mobile-spec-06-public-network-encrypted-connectivity.md`, `happy-client-mobile-plan.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the contract additive and LAN-first. The desktop pairing/token path remains authoritative for relay metadata, mobile only opts into relay when both the endpoint and secret are present, and the encrypted frame wrapper reuses the existing gateway command semantics so `SPEC-07` and later terminal work can layer on top without another transport reset.

### refactor(happy-client): prune mobile product routes and remove legacy auth bootstrap

- What changed: Reworked the `happy-client` root bootstrap so `happy-client/sources/app/_layout.tsx` no longer imports `AuthProvider`, `TokenStorage`, or `syncRestore`, and now only warms the persisted GhoDex device session through a dedicated `ghodex/appShell` bootstrap helper. Added route-surface guards in `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/_layout.tsx` so production now allows only `Workspace`, `Device`, `Settings`, and `Settings/Language`, while `dev/*` stays reachable only under `__DEV__`. Narrowed `happy-client/sources/components/CommandPalette/CommandPaletteProvider.tsx` to the same GhoDex-only navigation surface so it no longer depends on auth/logout, recent Happy sessions, or `/new`. Then physically deleted the legacy Expo Router pages for `artifacts`, `friends`, `inbox`, `machine`, `new`, `restore`, `server`, `session`, `terminal`, `user`, extra `settings/*`, `changelog`, and `text-selection`, leaving only the GhoDex routes plus `dev/*` inside `sources/app/(app)`. Also renamed the mobile package metadata and pairing client identifier from `ghodex-happy-client` to `ghodex-remote-client`. Added `happy-client/sources/ghodex/routes.ts` plus a focused Vitest spec to lock the allowlist and route normalization rules.
- Why: The plan's first dependency edge is correct: route pruning without bootstrap simplification would still leave the old Happy auth/sync platform running in the background, while removing the auth provider first without blocking legacy pages would leave direct route access paths that crash or revive upstream assumptions.
- Impact: Cold launch no longer revives the upstream account stack just to render the GhoDex remote client, the file-based route tree itself is now reduced to the intended GhoDex surface instead of merely being masked at runtime, command/search entry points no longer offer legacy Happy navigation, and the remaining production-facing mobile metadata no longer advertises the old client identity.
- Verification: `git diff --check -- happy-client/package.json happy-client/sources/app/_layout.tsx 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/_layout.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)' happy-client/sources/components/CommandPalette/CommandPaletteProvider.tsx happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx happy-client/sources/ghodex/appShell.ts happy-client/sources/ghodex/routes.ts happy-client/sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts CHANGELOG.md`; `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts sources/sync/settings.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`
- Files: `happy-client/package.json`, `happy-client/sources/app/_layout.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/_layout.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/*`, `happy-client/sources/components/CommandPalette/CommandPaletteProvider.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/appShell.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/routes.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Use the route guard first to keep the product stable while cutting over, then follow with physical file deletion once the kept routes and command entry points were isolated. That sequence satisfies the plan's dependency chain without taking a single risky all-or-nothing delete-first pass.

### refactor(happy-client): strip device connection fields out of app settings

- What changed: Added an explicit reserved-key filter in `happy-client/sources/sync/settings.ts` so GhoDex connection fields such as `host`, `port`, `pairingCode`, `authToken`, `deviceId`, and related transport/binding keys are removed during both `settingsParse()` and `applySettings()`. Extended `happy-client/sources/sync/settings.spec.ts` with coverage that keeps forward-compatible unknown fields while dropping reserved connection fields from both persisted settings payloads and in-memory merges.
- Why: The settings layer intentionally preserves unknown fields for compatibility, but that same behavior would silently keep any mistakenly written connection data in the app-preferences store, violating the plan's single-source-of-truth rule for device state.
- Impact: Theme/language and other app preferences remain forward-compatible, while device binding and transport state are now prevented from leaking into the settings persistence path even if an old screen or future regression tries to write them there.
- Verification: `git diff --check -- happy-client/sources/sync/settings.ts happy-client/sources/sync/settings.spec.ts CHANGELOG.md`; `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts sources/sync/settings.spec.ts`; `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`
- Files: `happy-client/sources/sync/settings.ts`, `happy-client/sources/sync/settings.spec.ts`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the compatibility-preserving unknown-field policy, but carve out a small explicit blacklist for connection metadata that must never be duplicated outside `ghodex/storage.ts`. That enforces rule B without turning the entire settings schema into a closed world.

### refactor(ghodex): add mobile device identity and desktop binding foundation

- What changed: Extended `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts` so the stored mobile session now carries `deviceId`, `deviceLabel`, `desktopId`, `desktopLabel`, `preferredDesktopId`, and `transportMode` alongside the existing LAN gateway credentials. The storage layer now auto-seeds and persists a stable local `deviceId` on first load, preserves that device identity when the user clears a saved pairing, and resets only the desktop binding fields during `clearStoredSession()`. Updated `happy-client/sources/ghodex/types.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/gateway.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/sessionState.ts`, and `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx` so pairing exchange can absorb optional desktop identity and transport metadata from the gateway response without breaking today's LAN flow when those fields are absent. On desktop, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessAuth.swift` now persists a stable `desktop_id` / `desktop_label` in control-harness auth state and includes that identity in pairing exchange plus token status responses, while `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift` adds coverage for stable identity issuance and reload persistence.
- Why: The original session model was only `host + token`, which was enough for the current LAN control path but not enough to support the plan's next steps around stable 1:1 desktop binding, future desktop-side device registry, and later relay/public transport layering.
- Impact: The phone now has a durable local identity foundation that survives pairing resets, and the stored session schema is now backed by an authoritative desktop identity emitted by the desktop harness itself. Current QR/manual LAN pairing remains compatible because missing future fields still sanitize back to safe defaults, while new pairings gain a stable 1:1 desktop binding contract that survives desktop app relaunches.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `cd happy-client && yarn test sources/ghodex/routes.spec.ts sources/sync/settings.spec.ts`; `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -derivedDataPath /tmp/ghodex-spec05-deriveddata -destination 'platform=macOS' -skip-testing:GhosttyUITests -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authPairingExchangeReturnsStableDesktopIdentity -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests/authRestoresDesktopIdentityAcrossReload test`

- Decision trail: Keep the first identity step local-first and backward-compatible, but let desktop auth own the authoritative desktop identity instead of introducing a second persistence silo. That lets mobile persist stable identity and preferred-desktop metadata now, while later registry and relay specs can reuse the same contract instead of renegotiating identity again.

### fix(build): make CEF-enabled macOS builds link sqlite and honor runtime architecture

- What changed: Updated `macos/build.nu` so Browser-enabled builds now inject `GHODEX_CEF_OTHER_LDFLAGS=-lsqlite3` and automatically narrow the app build to the runtime's compatible architecture when the installed CEF lane is single-arch. Synced the Xcode project defaults so raw `xcodebuild` flows no longer start from an empty CEF link flag set, and documented the required direct-build parameters in `README.md` and `AGENTS.md`.
- Why: The CEF bridge now uses SQLite APIs, but the supported build path was still clearing `GHODEX_CEF_OTHER_LDFLAGS`, which caused link failures until someone manually added `-lsqlite3`. At the same time, the managed codec-enabled runtime lane is arm64-only, while the default Xcode invocation still attempted a broader build, which produced avoidable architecture mismatches.
- Impact: The supported `nu macos/build.nu` path now builds a Browser-capable app without ad-hoc linker surgery, and it aligns the host app slice with the installed CEF runtime automatically when the runtime is single-arch. Low-level `xcodebuild` users also get a correct default sqlite link baseline plus explicit documented guidance for runtime-arch matching.
- Verification: `git diff --check`; `nu macos/build.nu --configuration ReleaseLocal --action build`; `codesign --verify --deep --strict macos/build/ReleaseLocal/GhoDex.app`; `lipo -info macos/build/ReleaseLocal/GhoDex.app/Contents/MacOS/GhoDex`
- Files: `macos/build.nu`, `macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj`, `README.md`, `AGENTS.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the runtime-specific policy in `macos/build.nu`, because that is the supported build entrypoint and the right place to inspect the installed CEF artifacts before compile. Keep project-level sqlite defaults in Xcode as a safety net for direct builds, but leave runtime-architecture resolution in the scripted path where the runtime on disk can be examined.

### fix(build): default main app builds to fail fast on missing CEF support

- What changed: Updated `macos/build.nu` so the main `GhoDex` app build now defaults to `CEF required` instead of silently downgrading to `GHODEX_CEF_ENABLED=0` when the configured runtime is missing. Added an explicit `--cef-mode auto|required|optional|disabled` switch, with `auto` resolving to `required` for the main app and `disabled` for non-browser targets. Added matching internal agent guidance in `AGENTS.md`, updated `README.md` source-build instructions to explain the Browser/CEF default behavior and runtime prerequisites, and refreshed `browser-tab-runtime-activation.md` so the docs match the new fail-fast path.
- Why: The previous scripted build flow only inspected the runtime on disk and quietly compiled an `unsupportedBuild` app when the runtime was missing. That let Browser-related work appear merged in source while the actual app bundle still launched without Chromium support, and it gave no compile-time reminder that CEF-specific build intent had been lost.
- Impact: Normal macOS app builds now align with the Browser-capable product expectation by default. If the runtime root is missing `Chromium Embedded Framework.framework` or the matching `libcef_dll_wrapper.a`, the build stops immediately with a clear explanation instead of shipping a confusing half-enabled Browser shell. Browser-disabled builds remain possible, but they must now be explicit.
- Verification: `git diff --check`; `nu macos/build.nu --help`; `GHODEX_CEF_ROOT=/tmp/ghx-missing-cef nu macos/build.nu --scheme GhoDex --configuration Debug --action clean` should fail with the new CEF gate message.
- Files: `macos/build.nu`, `AGENTS.md`, `README.md`, `browser-tab-runtime-activation.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the authoritative enforcement in `macos/build.nu`, because that is the supported macOS app build entrypoint and the only place that can evaluate runtime paths before compile. Keep raw Xcode defaults as lower-level knobs, but document clearly that the supported build path is fail-fast and Browser-capable by default.

### docs(browser): explain runtime activation gates and unsupported-build troubleshooting

- What changed: Added `browser-tab-runtime-activation.md` to document the two separate Browser activation gates: the app binary must be built with CEF host support, and a compatible runtime must exist at the configured runtime root. The doc now explains why a Browser tab can still render its shell while showing `compiled without managed Chromium runtime support`, why a CEF-enabled worktree build can succeed while a merged `main` app still fails, and how that differs from later H.264/AAC runtime capability questions. Linked `browser-tab-codec-runtime-playbook.md` back to this activation doc so build-vs-runtime confusion is resolved before codec work starts.
- Why: Browser development had already encoded the right runtime states in product code, but the durable docs still skipped the most operationally important distinction: source merge does not equal CEF-enabled app binary, and runtime installation does not repair an `unsupportedBuild` binary. That gap was causing repeated confusion during Browser rollout.
- Impact: Later agents and operators now have one durable explanation for the exact failure shown by the Browser tab when the host-build gate is missing. This should reduce wasted codec/runtime debugging on binaries that never enabled CEF in the first place.
- Verification: `git diff --check`
- Files: `browser-tab-runtime-activation.md`, `browser-tab-codec-runtime-playbook.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep the explanation in a dedicated runtime-activation doc instead of burying it inside the codec playbook or changelog alone. The recurring confusion is architectural, not codec-specific, so it needs a stable document that cleanly separates host-build, runtime-supply, and codec-capability layers.

### feat(build): expose verifiable app build fingerprints in About and bundle metadata

- What changed: Added build fingerprint metadata to the macOS app bundle, including commit, branch, build configuration, UTC build timestamp, workspace state, and a copyable fingerprint string. Updated the About panel to display those fields directly, fixed the commit link to point at the actual GitHub commit page, and taught both `macos/build.nu` and the Zig-driven macOS build path to inject the metadata during `xcodebuild`.
- Why: Version number alone cannot prove which local build is currently installed, especially when the same SemVer can be rebuilt more than once. The app needed a durable, user-visible identity for each build artifact.
- Impact: You can now verify from inside GhoDex whether `/Applications/GhoDex.app` is the specific build you asked for, and `defaults read ... GhoDexBuild` exposes the same fingerprint for terminal-side checks. The macOS build wrapper also refreshes the xcframework incrementally on every app build instead of trusting a stale mode marker.
- Verification: `nu macos/build.nu --configuration Release --action build`; `defaults read macos/build/Release/GhoDex.app/Contents/Info GhoDexBuild`; `defaults read macos/build/Release/GhoDex.app/Contents/Info GhoDexCommit`; open the About window and confirm fingerprint/commit/configuration/timestamp rows render.
- Files: `macos/build.nu`, `src/build/GhosttyXcodebuild.zig`, `src/build/GitVersion.zig`, `macos/GhoDex-Info.plist`, `macos/Sources/Features/About/AboutView.swift`, `macos/Sources/Helpers/AppLocalization.swift`, `macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Put the verification data in the app bundle, not only in logs or release notes, so the running app can identify itself. Keep the fingerprint generation at build time and surface it in the About window because that is the most direct place for a user to verify the installed artifact.

### chore(release): enforce VERSION-driven sync and push-time version gates

- What changed: Added `scripts/version_gate.py` to sync and validate the repo's version state, promoted root `VERSION` to the single source of truth, kept `macos/build.nu` as a lightweight sync gate that injects the synced version into Xcode builds, added a stricter `check-push` mode that compares outgoing commits against the upstream/base branch, updated the root `AGENTS.md` to require bumps only for ship-worthy pushes, and advanced the project version baseline to `0.1.1` across `VERSION`, `build.zig.zon`, and the Xcode project settings.
- Why: The project was carrying conflicting version sources (`VERSION`, `build.zig.zon`, and Xcode build settings), which let release artifacts report stale bundle versions. At the same time, forcing a fresh version bump before every compile would be unnecessary process friction.
- Impact: Future GhoDex builds now have one authoritative version path, local iteration builds stay low-friction, and the hard version bump requirement moves to the push/release boundary where it belongs.
- Verification: `python3 scripts/version_gate.py check`; `python3 scripts/version_gate.py check-push --base origin/main`; `python3 scripts/version_gate.py show`; `nu macos/build.nu --configuration Release --action build`; `defaults read macos/build/Release/GhoDex.app/Contents/Info CFBundleShortVersionString`; `defaults read macos/build/Release/GhoDex.app/Contents/Info CFBundleVersion`
- Files: `scripts/version_gate.py`, `macos/build.nu`, `AGENTS.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `VERSION`, `build.zig.zon`, `macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj`
- Decision trail: Keep the release version in one root file and make the build consume that source, rather than trusting multiple manually edited version fields to stay aligned. The hard enforcement point should be immediately before push/release, not before every compile, because that preserves accurate shipped history without slowing down local iteration.

### feat(happy-client): unify device controls and theme-aware device surfaces

- What changed: Reworked the `happy-client` GhoDex device flow so `/gateway` becomes a single `Device` center that owns QR pairing, saved pairing state, desktop machine access, account-device linking, connection endpoint tuning, sync mode, manual fallback pairing, and device reset. The old `/pairing` route now redirects into that unified device page. Updated the GhoDex workspace sidebar so `Device` opens the device center while `Settings` goes back to real app settings, and updated the command palette device action to the same destination. Replaced the accidental upstream HappyCode settings landing page with a lightweight GhoDex settings screen, so the main `Settings` entry now keeps only GhoDex-owned app controls such as black/white theme switching and app language instead of showing support, GitHub, Claude, and other upstream-only integrations. Removed the stale command-palette entry that still navigated into the upstream account page, and normalized the language settings page to the same black/white theme tokens. Switched the GhoDex workspace, device pages, shared lists, and related settings surfaces to the shared light/dark theme tokens, and changed the default local theme preference to `dark` so new installs stay visually aligned with the existing dark workspace. Hardened startup by mounting `AuthProvider` in the app root, restoring saved credentials during bootstrap, timing out the first ready gate instead of waiting forever for initial sync success, timing out stored device-session reads, and redirecting malformed session routes back to `/`. Updated the Android Gradle React Native config so the normal `installDebug` path embeds the JS bundle, while `debugOptimized` remains the Metro-dependent development lane.
- Why: The previous structure split device management across a dark workspace, a light gateway settings page, and a separate pairing page, which made the app feel visually inconsistent and mixed device responsibilities into a generic settings surface. The gateway endpoint still matters as an advanced fallback for adb reverse, LAN pairing, and future multi-device topologies, but it should live under device management rather than masquerading as a standalone settings page. During the first pass, the `Settings` entry was mistakenly left wired to HappyCode's upstream settings shell, which replaced the intended GhoDex page with controls that do not actually configure this product. On top of that, rebuild/cold-start flows were coupling first paint to successful initial sync and auth bootstrap, which made transient startup failures look like a permanent loading screen. Separately, direct `app:installDebug` adb installs were still producing a debug build that expected Metro, so the app could sit behind the splash screen with `Unable to load script` even after a successful rebuild/install.
- Impact: Device pairing and connection management now live behind one stable entry point, the saved QR result remains the durable default path, and the device/settings boundary is clearer in the GhoDex workspace. The main `Settings` page is back to being a GhoDex-owned app-preferences surface instead of an upstream HappyCode shell, and the first settings layer now stays aligned with the black/white theme direction you wanted. Rebuilds and cold starts should no longer strand the app on a perpetual loading screen just because the first sync pass, auth restore, or SecureStore read is slow, and direct Android debug installs should now launch without requiring an active Metro session.
- Verification: `cd happy-client && yarn typecheck`; `git diff --check -- 'happy-client/android/app/build.gradle' 'happy-client/sources/app/_layout.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/session/[id].tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/index.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/language.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/components/CommandPalette/CommandPaletteProvider.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/components/SettingsView.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/components/ItemList.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/auth/AuthContext.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts' 'happy-client/sources/unistyles.ts' 'happy-client/sources/sync/sync.ts' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/appearance.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/account.tsx' 'happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/connect/claude.tsx' CHANGELOG.md`; `cd happy-client/android && ANDROID_HOME="$HOME/Library/Android/sdk" ANDROID_SDK_ROOT="$HOME/Library/Android/sdk" ./gradlew app:installDebug`; cold-launch the app on device and confirm logcat no longer reports `Unable to load script`.
- Files: `happy-client/android/app/build.gradle`, `happy-client/sources/app/_layout.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/_layout.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/gateway.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/pairing.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/index.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/session/[id].tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/index.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/account.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/appearance.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/connect/claude.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/app/(app)/settings/language.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/auth/AuthContext.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/components/CommandPalette/CommandPaletteProvider.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/components/ItemList.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/components/SettingsView.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/storage.ts`, `happy-client/sources/ghodex/ui.tsx`, `happy-client/sources/sync/localSettings.ts`, `happy-client/sources/sync/sync.ts`, `happy-client/sources/unistyles.ts`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Collapse the duplicated pairing/settings surfaces instead of trying to keep three partially overlapping pages in sync. Keep endpoint and manual pairing available, but demote them to advanced device controls while making QR scan plus saved session retention the primary mental model. Treat account-device linking as device management too, so it belongs under `Device` instead of `Settings > Account`, and keep the theme UI aligned around a simple black/white switch rather than mixed adaptive and fixed-theme behaviors. For Android delivery, preserve one Metro-based lane in `debugOptimized`, but make the default `installDebug` path self-contained because this repo's normal phone-install workflow should not require a separate bundler process just to get past the splash screen.

### fix(control-harness): bound retained read frames and clean terminal teardown state

- What changed: Reworked `ControlHarnessTerminalReadStore` so retained frames now store only canonical `content` text instead of both `content` and a persistent `[String]` line cache, added terminal-scoped cleanup on close, and enforced global retention guards with max frame count and max total retained text bytes on top of the existing per-key frame cap. Added matching `ControlHarnessReadAfterWriteStore` terminal cleanup and regression tests covering teardown and global eviction behavior.
- Why: The harness read path was retaining historical terminal snapshots in memory across repeated reads and terminal churn, which let `MALLOC_SMALL` grow without a process-wide bound and made closed terminals keep contributing to memory usage.
- Impact: Continuous harness reads now have bounded in-process retention, closed terminals release their cached read state promptly, and repeated read/snapshot workflows fall back to reset semantics after eviction instead of silently growing memory toward tens of gigabytes.
- Verification: `xcodebuild -project macos/GhoDex.xcodeproj -scheme GhoDex -destination 'platform=macOS' -only-testing:GhosttyTests/ControlHarnessTests test`
- Files: `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessSupport.swift`, `macos/Sources/Features/Control Harness/ControlHarnessCore.swift`, `macos/Tests/ControlHarness/ControlHarnessTests.swift`, `CHANGELOG.md`
- Decision trail: Keep frame retention in memory for low-latency delta/window reads, but bound it at the store layer so callers do not need to manage cache safety themselves. Prefer evicting old snapshots and resetting client deltas over preserving unlimited historical frames.

### feat(browser): add codec runtime build and managed acceptance tooling

- What changed: Extended `scripts/install_cef_runtime.sh` so it can write runtime `manifest.json` and `managed-runtime.json` metadata for `ffmpegBranding`, `proprietaryCodecs`, and `mediaCapabilities` instead of only copying a bare CEF bundle. Added `scripts/build_codec_enabled_cef_runtime.sh`, a repo-owned official CEF `automate-git.py` wrapper that builds an arm64 codec-enabled distribution with `proprietary_codecs=true` and `ffmpeg_branding=Chrome`, then installs it into GhoDex's managed runtime root. `scripts/browser_media_debug_acceptance.py` can now validate a runtime staged through an isolated app-support `CEF/current` plus `managed-runtime.json`, so the managed-runtime lane can be exercised without forcing `GHODEX_CEF_ROOT`. Added `browser-tab-codec-runtime-playbook.md` to record the end-to-end supply workflow.
- Why: The Browser codebase had already been reduced to a supply-side blocker, but the repo still lacked a durable way to produce a codec-enabled runtime, stamp the metadata that GhoDex understands, and validate that runtime through the same managed path the product will actually use.
- Impact: The H.264/AAC blocker is no longer "find a mystery third-party archive." GhoDex now has a repo-owned build/install/acceptance path for a codec-enabled CEF runtime. The remaining uncertainty is host-side execution evidence: run the official build on a machine with enough disk/build prerequisites, then rerun the media probe against the resulting artifact.
- Verification: `bash -n scripts/install_cef_runtime.sh scripts/build_codec_enabled_cef_runtime.sh`, `python3 -m py_compile scripts/browser_media_debug_acceptance.py`, `scripts/install_cef_runtime.sh --source /tmp/ghx-cef-runtime-installer-smoke/cef_binary_145.0.28+g51162e8+chromium-145.0.7632.160_macosarm64.tar.gz --destination /tmp/ghx-cef-runtime-installer-smoke/install-root-archive --slug codec-enabled-smoke-archive --runtime-source codec-enabled-smoke-archive --ffmpeg-branding Chrome --proprietary-codecs true --media-h264 true --media-aac true --managed-descriptor /tmp/ghx-cef-runtime-installer-smoke/install-root-archive/managed-runtime.json`, `python3 scripts/browser_media_debug_acceptance.py --app /tmp/ghx-cef-media-build/Debug/GhoDex.app --managed-runtime-root /tmp/ghx-cef-runtime-installer-smoke/install-root-archive/current --managed-runtime-descriptor /tmp/ghx-cef-runtime-installer-smoke/install-root-archive/managed-runtime.json --mode managed --output /tmp/ghx-browser-media-debug-managed-runtime-copy.json`, `scripts/build_codec_enabled_cef_runtime.sh --work-root /tmp/ghx-codec-build-dry-run --managed-descriptor /tmp/ghx-codec-build-dry-run/managed-runtime.json --dry-run`
